    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3265201351003831085">Delrita likes being invisible. If no one notices her, then no one willnotice her uncle Punky either. Punky is a grown man with a child's mind. Delrita loves him dearly and can't stand people making fun of his Down Syndrome. But when tragedy strikes, Delrita's quiet life— and Punky's— are disrupted forever. Can she finally learn to trust others, for her own sake and Punky's</span>
  <span id="freeText3265201351003831085" style="display:none">Delrita likes being invisible. If no one notices her, then no one willnotice her uncle Punky either. Punky is a grown man with a child's mind. Delrita loves him dearly and can't stand people making fun of his Down Syndrome. But when tragedy strikes, Delrita's quiet life— and Punky's— are disrupted forever. Can she finally learn to trust others, for her own sake and Punky's? This story captures the joy and sorrow that come when we open our hearts to love. <p>Author Biography: June Rae Wood lives near Windsor, Missouri.</p></span>

<div id="review_15535474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15535474" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/912789-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417720619p2/912789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15535474?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate" href="/user/show/912789-nate">Nate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15535474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5987605716661134062">Ok well, this one took me some time before I got up enough guts to read. I am into fantasy and sci-fi books; I do not love clowns, but I don’t hate them either. The book cover’s McDonald’s color scheme didn’t really grab my attention either. However, I thought I should give it a try, remember what they say, “You shouldn’t judge a book by it’s cover.” <br/><br/>WOW, this was a very emotional, humbling, and uplifting book. I am NOT an overly emotional person, but my eyes did get a wee bit moist now and then</span>
  <span id="freeText5987605716661134062" style="display:none">Ok well, this one took me some time before I got up enough guts to read. I am into fantasy and sci-fi books; I do not love clowns, but I don’t hate them either. The book cover’s McDonald’s color scheme didn’t really grab my attention either. However, I thought I should give it a try, remember what they say, “You shouldn’t judge a book by it’s cover.” <br /><br />WOW, this was a very emotional, humbling, and uplifting book. I am NOT an overly emotional person, but my eyes did get a wee bit moist now and then – I think it was because I was eating some chips and super hot salsa at the time. Nevertheless, this book opened my eyes to those families who have to live and deal with disabilities. It reminded me that people with any type of disability are truly amazing people and deserve to be treated with love and respect. They should never be taken for granted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5987605716661134062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/7590687-kayla-dream-write-read">Kayla (Dream.Write.Read)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8970951-emily-polson?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2403399395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6574497477220950261">This is a really sweet middle grade read about a thirteen-year-old girl and her Uncle Punky, who has Down's syndrome. She struggles to make friends when her family moves into town because she wants to protect her uncle from people who might mock him. There's a lot of drama packed into its 200 pages, both life-altering events and fighting between friends. Great character development (if a bit predictable). The story handles an important topic really well (the author drew from her own relationship</span>
  <span id="freeText6574497477220950261" style="display:none">This is a really sweet middle grade read about a thirteen-year-old girl and her Uncle Punky, who has Down's syndrome. She struggles to make friends when her family moves into town because she wants to protect her uncle from people who might mock him. There's a lot of drama packed into its 200 pages, both life-altering events and fighting between friends. Great character development (if a bit predictable). The story handles an important topic really well (the author drew from her own relationship with her brother who has Down's syndrome). I'd definitely recommend it to MG readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6574497477220950261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_482801208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482801208" />
    <a title="Sarah Wolters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12958235-sarah-wolters"><img alt="Sarah Wolters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460177281p2/12958235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Wolters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Wolters" href="/user/show/12958235-sarah-wolters">Sarah Wolters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482801208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5383934121269344869">This book is one of my absolute favourites. It's both heartwarming and heart wrenching at the same time. Delrita's character is very shy and quiet, and with me being the same way, she was very easy to relate to. Wood writes about Delrita's relationship with her Uncle Punky, who has Down's Syndrome, and how Delrita deals with the troubles that she has with the kids at school in a realistic and interesting way, which makes the book a worthwhile read. It is a relatively short book, but the story it</span>
  <span id="freeText5383934121269344869" style="display:none">This book is one of my absolute favourites. It's both heartwarming and heart wrenching at the same time. Delrita's character is very shy and quiet, and with me being the same way, she was very easy to relate to. Wood writes about Delrita's relationship with her Uncle Punky, who has Down's Syndrome, and how Delrita deals with the troubles that she has with the kids at school in a realistic and interesting way, which makes the book a worthwhile read. It is a relatively short book, but the story it contains is a long and heavy one. I would recommend this book to pretty much anyone, as well as reading the sequel, Turtle on a Fence Post. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5383934121269344869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2064038718450858672">I read this book back in elementary school, and it was my first "real" book. I found myself disliking Aunt Queenie more than once, but near the end of the book a new side came out and it just added a sense of happiness to the book. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4149638219585336058">A sweet book with lots of possibulity of growth, personal insights, and the teacher in me found so much I would want to discuss with young readers. <br/><br/>Delrita lives with her mom and dad, and her uncle "Punky", who lives with Down's syndrome. Family life revolves around sheltering Punky from possible ridicule for his disabilities. Everyone is used to Punky yelling, "Bang" at the end of prayers, his habit of storing chicken bones behind the TV, his obsession with clowns, and his irrepressible mouth. </span>
  <span id="freeText4149638219585336058" style="display:none">A sweet book with lots of possibulity of growth, personal insights, and the teacher in me found so much I would want to discuss with young readers. <br /><br />Delrita lives with her mom and dad, and her uncle "Punky", who lives with Down's syndrome. Family life revolves around sheltering Punky from possible ridicule for his disabilities. Everyone is used to Punky yelling, "Bang" at the end of prayers, his habit of storing chicken bones behind the TV, his obsession with clowns, and his irrepressible mouth. He says exactly what's on his mind, even when that embarrasses others. Everyone is used to Punky except Aunt Queenie...she wants to take control, to move Punky into a group home, get him a job in the workshop. Delrita and her mother are committed to keeping Punky at home, away from prying eyes. Delrita does everything she can to become invisible...because if she is, then no one can make fun of Punky.<br /><br />Delrita and Punky are forced into a life neither of them want. Too many changes break the precarious balance, and Delrita is forced to learn there are other ways to SEE Punky, and her own life. She must come to terms with the changes Aunt Queenie is pushing. <br /><br />A tear-jerker, for sure...Delrita navigates the life she never asked for, and sees Punky's promise and gifts as she learns slowly to be seen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4149638219585336058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sssnoo reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sssnoo reads" href="/user/show/38024473-sssnoo-reads">sssnoo reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8392895-the-man-who-loved-clowns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38024473-sssnoo-reads?shelf=50-states-challenge-2018">50-states-challenge-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38024473-sssnoo-reads?shelf=region-us">region-us</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555709643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7804711925069776633">I know this book was written in 1992, and I realize it is a young adult book, but I had some issues with its depiction of Down Syndrome. First and foremost HOW has the editing over the years not corrected the author’s use of Down’s for Down. Many lay people make the error, but the author describes her family member with Down Syndrome so she should be aware and there WERE editors in 1992. Also, this book was just too formulaic for me. While I appreciate how the author wrote Punky’s character, Del</span>
  <span id="freeText7804711925069776633" style="display:none">I know this book was written in 1992, and I realize it is a young adult book, but I had some issues with its depiction of Down Syndrome. First and foremost HOW has the editing over the years not corrected the author’s use of Down’s for Down. Many lay people make the error, but the author describes her family member with Down Syndrome so she should be aware and there WERE editors in 1992. Also, this book was just too formulaic for me. While I appreciate how the author wrote Punky’s character, Delrita was just annoying. So was her mother. I suppose their level of stubbornnes and self flagelating was on purpose so the author could use them to create the conflict she needed for the story - butit was too extreme and annoying. I wanted to shake Delrita and barely felt compassion for her. I sound harsh, but this book has an average rating well over 4 and I do not get it. <br /><br />Missouri checked off my 50-state challenge. I will have to find something better next trip.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7804711925069776633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4167211715632446375">Forewarning: You will cry.<br/><br/>I'm honestly surprised that this book is not more popular. It is beautiful.<br/><br/>My only real critiques are these: (1) I dislike how it is inferred that Delrita's mother didn't love or care for Punky as much as Aunt Queenie. Neither way of "raising" Punky was wrong. They were just different.   <span id="freeText4167211715632446375" style="display:none">Forewarning: You will cry.<br /><br />I'm honestly surprised that this book is not more popular. It is beautiful.<br /><br />My only real critiques are these: (1) I dislike how it is inferred that Delrita's mother didn't love or care for Punky as much as Aunt Queenie. Neither way of "raising" Punky was wrong. They were just different. I do believe Delrita's mother should have been more open to the workshop or at least researched it more, but at the same time, Aunt Queenie should have understood that her approach of the idea was wrong and was putting everyone off the idea.<br /><br />And (2) I wish there had been clearer resolution between Delrita and the Shacklefords. I know resolution is implied, but I wanted to see both the girls learn to listen to the whole story before passing judgement, and I wanted to see what was going to happen between Delrita and Tree.<br /><br />Otherwise, I highly recommend this book.</span>

<div id="review_3286499468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3286499468" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113133916-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3286499468?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/113133916-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113133916-karen?shelf=tween-chapter-books">tween-chapter-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3286499468&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3286499468" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6389403788512928191">The Man Who Loved Clowns by Juna Rae Wood tells the story of 13 year old Delrita and her Uncle Punky who has down syndrome who she deeply cares about. When her parents pass, she learns to open her doors and let people into her life as well as Punkys. The book is based on the author and her brother who has down syndrome as well, and that is very evident because the way she describes Punky’s actions and feelings are very accurate. This book will make you cry! It is a great book to have in classroo</span>
  <span id="freeText6389403788512928191" style="display:none">The Man Who Loved Clowns by Juna Rae Wood tells the story of 13 year old Delrita and her Uncle Punky who has down syndrome who she deeply cares about. When her parents pass, she learns to open her doors and let people into her life as well as Punkys. The book is based on the author and her brother who has down syndrome as well, and that is very evident because the way she describes Punky’s actions and feelings are very accurate. This book will make you cry! It is a great book to have in classrooms because it shows how people should treat each other with kindness despite differences. This book came to me at the perfect time, I was also thirteen when I first read it and my little brother who also has down syndrome was starting school for the first time. I was nervous for him and didn’t want him to go and this book perfectly encapsulates that time for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6389403788512928191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E0RdrKGcsbbFK1rS1QZCJdkGhFqWwvQEja6n9YiAFYQrlVvuIC6yCYyDNT/N8pITWqFMGgsy4w5A/Cf0cZa53w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('luy0QkGuYo8VQgUFuSsaHmHFuwjTNuqUJ0Tjfqtg8pauPbIAwBxhMFzqauih38oo4mJzSE7G/Z7qFmN/UnZezQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/22961.June_Rae_Wood">About June Rae Wood</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/22961.June_Rae_Wood"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1242836228p3/22961.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/22961.June_Rae_Wood">June Rae Wood
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12199879550431703859">June Rae Wood, the author of the famous <u>
  <i>The Man WHo Loved Clowns </i>
</u>, was born in 1946 in <b>
  <i>Sedalia, Missouri</i>
</b>. "My brother Richard was born [in 1948] with Down's syndrome and a heart defect," author June Rae Wood wrote in the Sedalia Democrat in 1995. "The doctor said he wouldn't live, and even if he did, he would never walk or talk. He advised my parents to send Richard to die in an institutio</span>
  <span id="freeText12199879550431703859" style="display:none">June Rae Wood, the author of the famous <u>
  <i>The Man WHo Loved Clowns </i>
</u>, was born in 1946 in <b>
  <i>Sedalia, Missouri</i>
</b>. "My brother Richard was born [in 1948] with Down's syndrome and a heart defect," author June Rae Wood wrote in the Sedalia Democrat in 1995. "The doctor said he wouldn't live, and even if he did, he would never walk or talk. He advised my parents to send Richard to die in an institution, rather than take him home and let the family get attached to him." Wood, the second of what would eventually be eight children, was only two years old when her parents brought Richard, their third child, home from the hospital. Although her parents gave all their children special attention, Richard, whom Wood's mother called her little "Dickey-bird," was doted on and protected by all the family members. This was not just because he was handicapped, but also because Richard was very special to them all. He would eventually become the subject of Wood's award-winning first book, The Man Who Loved Clowns. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12199879550431703859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
